  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_430cc109-749f-4de6-a166-2e171eb35355'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16505134183092421216">The Little Dog and other stories.<br/>Comprising four very different adult, speculative, spiritual and philosophical novellas to intrigue, entertain and and keep you guessing. <br/><br/>The Little Dog – a story of good and evil and retribution.<br/><br/>Bill, a retired forester, recounts a week in his early working life when he was paired with an unsavoury workmate.   <span id="freeText16505134183092421216" style="display:none">The Little Dog and other stories.<br />Comprising four very different adult, speculative, spiritual and philosophical novellas to intrigue, entertain and and keep you guessing. <br /><br />The Little Dog – a story of good and evil and retribution.<br /><br />Bill, a retired forester, recounts a week in his early working life when he was paired with an unsavoury workmate. This commences with them finding a little domestic dog sitting beside a forest haul-road way out in a remote part of the forest, but what is a little dog doing in such an unlikely location? As the week goes on it becomes increasingly uncomfortable, the little dog disappears, events take an unexpected turn and our young troubled and naive Bill starts to learn some awful truths. <br /><br />The Golden Tup - a dreadful tale of paradise being cruelly taken by latent evil.<br /><br />This tale opens with the shocking news that a nice young couple have killed their new born baby. How could they have done such a dreadful thing? Our narrator, Verity, recalls how the pair bought an old derelict farmhouse and commenced renovating it; creating their own paradise. However, their felling an old tree changed everything.<br /><br />The Crow - a poignant tale of misunderstanding, dying, bitterness and blame.<br /><br />As a child, David, is taken to a hospice by his mother where he finds himself listening to an increasingly mad tale told by a dying and embittered old Irish priest. But why do the old priest’s recollections of the school days and subsequent rise of a local councillor become so increasingly bizarre and bitter? <br /><br />The White Hart - a happy ghost story, if there can be such a thing!<br /><br />What might connect a chance encounter with a little albino deer, an equally unexpected meeting with a beautiful, but somewhat enigmatic young girl in a remote chapel, and a third, just as strange an incident, on a windswept hillside? Pete Montague, relates a redemptive, adult, speculative, spiritual and philosophical happy ghost story - if there can be such a thing! <br /><br />(Warning to sensitive readers; some tales do contain a tiny bit of bad language and references to sex)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16505134183092421216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2125063259" />
    <a title="Leigh Holland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66353759-leigh-holland"><img alt="Leigh Holland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490662296p2/66353759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2125063259?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leigh Holland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leigh Holland" href="/user/show/66353759-leigh-holland">Leigh Holland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2125063259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13797906272248755378">The Red Grouse Tales: The Little Dog and Other Stories by Leslie W P Garland, 358 pages, December 2nd 2015, Genre: Contemporary Fiction. Warning: May Contain Spoilers.<br/><br/>Review by Leigh Holland.<br/><br/>The Red Grouse Tales is a collection of four novellas into a larger work. Each tale is tied together by style and theme. The style of the work is first person storytelling narration. A person is telling the story to another person for the duration of each tale. This is my least favorite style, but that’s a p</span>
  <span id="freeText13797906272248755378" style="display:none">The Red Grouse Tales: The Little Dog and Other Stories by Leslie W P Garland, 358 pages, December 2nd 2015, Genre: Contemporary Fiction. Warning: May Contain Spoilers.<br /><br />Review by Leigh Holland.<br /><br />The Red Grouse Tales is a collection of four novellas into a larger work. Each tale is tied together by style and theme. The style of the work is first person storytelling narration. A person is telling the story to another person for the duration of each tale. This is my least favorite style, but that’s a personal preference. Others may like the way the stories are presented. <br />The theme that binds the tales together is the nature, origin, and manifestation of evil in our world. Each tale presents ‘evil’ in a different way and compels the reader to reflect on it. What is evil, truly? Can we know someone is ‘evil’? Is evil a sentient force striving to release itself and cover the world? Or is evil just a name we give to things that horrify us? How do we confront evil when others can’t see it for what it is?<br />Of the four tales, my favorite is the third one, “The Golden Tup”. In this tale, a couple having marital problems discovers a journal from one hundred and fifty years ago. The journal reveals information about an evil on their farmland. Once the couple agrees as to the place where evil dwells, what they do to remedy the situation is truly horrifying. Were they right? Or were they now “evil”?<br />Overall, I really liked the concept of each story. I think the style made it more difficult for me to really get into it. The stories weaved the theme well throughout the work and the style remained consistent. I'd rate this work 3.5 stars.<br /></span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153504440?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darque  Dreamer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darque  Dreamer " href="/user/show/63753159-darque-dreamer">Darque  Dreamer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153504440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17816760787410219184">The Red Grouse Tales is a collection of four intriguing, mysterious, campfire like tales. They are thought provoking, with hidden morals and lessons, and a hint of creepiness. These modern folk tales containing philosophical and religious nods are full of depth and dimension, and are definitely worth a read.<br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised by how much I enjoyed these tales. They are told, each by a separate person, in a group in a campfire type feel, as one would tell scary stories. Each tale began a </span>
  <span id="freeText17816760787410219184" style="display:none">The Red Grouse Tales is a collection of four intriguing, mysterious, campfire like tales. They are thought provoking, with hidden morals and lessons, and a hint of creepiness. These modern folk tales containing philosophical and religious nods are full of depth and dimension, and are definitely worth a read.<br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised by how much I enjoyed these tales. They are told, each by a separate person, in a group in a campfire type feel, as one would tell scary stories. Each tale began a little slow for me, but then picked up and intrigued me to keep reading. They were deceptively beautiful and full of mystery. They were enchanting and quite detailed. They offered lessons of morality and judgement, and touched on ideas of good vs. evil. They had supernatural aspects to them, and gave me chills several times, while reading them today, on Halloween. <br /><br />As a whole, I would rate this book 3.5-4 stars. I enjoyed each tale, despite their slow, long winded starts, and I was left deep in thought at the end of each one. The tales, though each unique, fit together seamlessly, and offered a sense of spine-tingling enchantment and intrigue.<br /><br />Thank you to the author for sending me this free e-copy in exchange for my honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2795050798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2795050798" />
    <a title="Debjani Ghosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59270235-debjani-ghosh"><img alt="Debjani Ghosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472914242p2/59270235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2795050798?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debjani Ghosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debjani Ghosh" href="/user/show/59270235-debjani-ghosh">Debjani Ghosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2795050798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer800271235171533664">[Reviewed for Readers' Favorite by Debjani Ghosh]<br/><br/><i>The Red Grouse Tales</i> by Leslie W P Garland is a unique collection of four spiritual, philosophical, and mysterious novellas tinged with an element of the supernatural. These stories are narrated by a group of people in a local pub. <i>The Little Dog</i> relays how karma works. Bill, now a retired forester, recounts the strange and disturbing incidents, which involved a cute little dog, that occurred during a week in his early working life. <i>The Crow</i> is a </span>
  <span id="freeText800271235171533664" style="display:none">[Reviewed for Readers' Favorite by Debjani Ghosh]<br /><br /><i>The Red Grouse Tales</i> by Leslie W P Garland is a unique collection of four spiritual, philosophical, and mysterious novellas tinged with an element of the supernatural. These stories are narrated by a group of people in a local pub. <i>The Little Dog</i> relays how karma works. Bill, now a retired forester, recounts the strange and disturbing incidents, which involved a cute little dog, that occurred during a week in his early working life. <i>The Crow</i> is a tale of misunderstanding, and above all, vanity. An old priest on his deathbed narrates the childhood and subsequent ascendancy of a local councilor, and how his involvement in the construction of a dam affected the valley. <i>The Golden Tup</i> shows the crumbling of paradise bit-by-bit. It chronicles the shocking story of why a young couple murdered their babe. In <i>The White Hart</i>, Pete Montague regales his audience with his chance encounter with a little albino deer and his subsequent meeting with an enchanting girl in a remote chapel.<br /><br />Each story in the <i>The Red Grouse Tales</i> is well-written, laden with beautiful imagery, and are hugely atmospheric. All the tales provide lush details of the respective quaint towns they are set in. Leslie W P Garland is a gifted storyteller. He provides distinct voices to the narrator and the different characters in the story. <i>The Crow</i> is an immersive tale and stresses how vanity can distort one's perception of reality. Out of all the stories, <i>The Golden Tup</i> was my favorite. The twist at the end was unexpected. <i>The White Hart</i> is another impressive addition to this collection.<br /><br />I wouldn’t say these stories make for quick reading. It took time for me to get used to the author's writing style but once I did, these stories were worth reading. The author often indulges into philosophical musings which enhance the stories. With just the hint of the paranormal, they explore the various vices of men. All the stories implore the reader to think about what is right and wrong. Biblical knowledge would help readers appreciate the stories more. <br /><br />I will recommend <i>The Red Grouse Tales</i> by Leslie W P Garland to fans of speculative fiction. People seeking something different from their usual dose of thrillers/crime fiction can also pick it up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="800271235171533664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11866663366903600518" style="display:none">I love short stories. With a busy life and little time to sit down, these stories fill a nice gap in the day. I found this book to be an immensely enjoyable read, with well planned and delivered stories. I particularly found The White Hart and The Little Dog to be great reads, and they were favourites. I loved Bill's relationship develop with the dog. The detailed and enchanting stories had a religious tone, which wouldn't be something I'd particularly choose, but however I found that the focus of this was mainly on impact and life decisions which is very true to life. <br /><br />The characters are brought to life by the author and each story is formed nicely in an easy to read manner. The author uses the accent and dialect well, although this became a little confusing and maybe overdone in 'The Crow', it gave an authentic feel to the delightfully portrayed characters. I found them to be an interesting collection of stories. For those that enjoy great novellas, I would recommend. I'd love to read more short stories by this author.</span>

<div id="review_3148390419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3148390419" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3148390419?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3148390419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5928669362864157382">Perspectives, perceptions, and human foibles<br/><br/>British author Leslie Garland is a Chartered Civil Engineer and has worked in the UK, the Far East and Africa in that role. Owning his own stock photograph library, he is a member of the Royal Photographic Society and the British Institute of Professional Photography and has written extensively for the trade press. Now he writes fiction, short stories such as this impressive collection – The Red Grouse Tales. He lives in Northumberland, England.<br/><br/>The app</span>
  <span id="freeText5928669362864157382" style="display:none">Perspectives, perceptions, and human foibles<br /><br />British author Leslie Garland is a Chartered Civil Engineer and has worked in the UK, the Far East and Africa in that role. Owning his own stock photograph library, he is a member of the Royal Photographic Society and the British Institute of Professional Photography and has written extensively for the trade press. Now he writes fiction, short stories such as this impressive collection – The Red Grouse Tales. He lives in Northumberland, England.<br /><br />The appeal of these four novellas is universal: each story takes on thoughtful questions and ideas we all ponder, but rarely discuss. The setting for his collection is placed in the Foreword, an entry step that is most inviting – ‘Quite how we’d got into this story telling is something that eludes me now, but somehow we had; the ‘we’ being a group of us who had met usually, though not exclusively, at The Red Grouse Inn on the first Thursday evening of each month. The Red Grouse was an old coaching inn run by a charming landlady called Jenny. She had been married once upon a time, but things hadn’t worked out and after her divorce she’d ended up buying the inn. It had a warm, cosy, homely feel to it - red carpets, dark oak wood panelling, benches with cushions and heavily varnished tables - and if you liked sitting round one of these tables and having a few pints of Jenny’s excellent real ale and a chat on an evening, then this was the place for you! Then, on one such evening, one of our company told a story. It came completely out of the blue, with no prior discussion or anything to suggest it would happen. What I do recall is that that first story, whichever one it was, had us all entranced, so much so that at the following meeting a story was almost expected and thereafter we started to look forward to those Thursday evenings not just for the social chit-chat, but for the story that we would hear that evening.’<br /><br />With that invitation to join in the tradition, Leslie distills each of the four stories as follows – ‘The Little Dog – a story of good and evil and retribution, The Crow - a poignant tale of misunderstanding, dying, bitterness and blame, The Golden Tup - a dreadful tale of paradise being cruelly taken by latent evil, The White Hart - a happy ghost story, if there can be such a thing!’<br /><br />Each story is rich in both content and execution, with a hefty dollop of charm and a soupçon of surreal and paranormal and philosophical and spiritual concepts. The prose is excellent and each story pleads to be a favorite of the collection – until the next one spills out. This is superb writing from a gifted man whose photography exposure radiates from his imagery and imagination. Highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5928669362864157382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14054624440854157401">Related as stories told between friends in the Red Grouse pub, each of these tales has a thread of the paranormal and philosophy running through them, to varying degrees. There are four stories to enjoy (I have also reviewed each of these separately in depth)<br/><br/>The Little Dog is the story of a forester who is forced to work with a much disliked colleague for a week. Each day is tense and stressful, but is Blackman just unsociable or actually evil?<br/><br/>The Crow focuses on a local politician, generally he</span>
  <span id="freeText14054624440854157401" style="display:none">Related as stories told between friends in the Red Grouse pub, each of these tales has a thread of the paranormal and philosophy running through them, to varying degrees. There are four stories to enjoy (I have also reviewed each of these separately in depth)<br /><br />The Little Dog is the story of a forester who is forced to work with a much disliked colleague for a week. Each day is tense and stressful, but is Blackman just unsociable or actually evil?<br /><br />The Crow focuses on a local politician, generally held in high regard but the tale of his life as related by a bitter and dying priest casts doubt on his motives.<br /><br />The Golden Tup is the tale of a local couple who are notorious for having killed their baby. But just perhaps not everything is as it seems. Has an old evil been awoken?<br /><br />The White Hart finishes the stories with a very rare thing - a heartwarming and feelgood ghost story that touches on the power that men wield over women, and vice versa.<br /><br />Each of these tales has a different tone but are a complete story in their own right, even if some make mention of places and events in others. The story telling makes this a great collection to dip into and read. As each story also carries a philosophical theme they have a depth and resonance beyond the actual tale being told.<br /><br />A good collection of paranormal and interesting stories, definitely worth a read.</span>

I read this through once myself and then read over a number of sitting to a (reasonably) young relative and he enjoyed it just as much as I had. This would also make a good candidate for a book club as many issues for discussion are thrown </span>
  <span id="freeText4024561645848131744" style="display:none">The four stories in the Red Grouse tales were as entertaining as they were charming, and overall a really fun read. The different narrators of the stories I felt gave each tale a unique nature, and they felt quite different to each other but still just a fun. I read this through once myself and then read over a number of sitting to a (reasonably) young relative and he enjoyed it just as much as I had. This would also make a good candidate for a book club as many issues for discussion are thrown up in each of the four stories.</span>

<div id="review_2210353383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2210353383" />
    <a title="Courtney Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6269034-courtney-thomas"><img alt="Courtney Thomas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210353383?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney Thomas" href="/user/show/6269034-courtney-thomas">Courtney Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2210353383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17528350904070792297">It was such a treat to read “The Red Grouse Tales” by Leslie W.P. Garland. The four short stories within this novel are thoroughly engaging contemporary allegories. I love John Milton’s “Paradise Lost,” thus I was delighted by how deftly Garland interweaves the well-known archangels into these modern-day tales. “The Red Grouse Tales” consists of the most well-done and effective frame narratives I have come across in contemporary pieces of literature. Even more to Garland’s credit, I never consid</span>
  <span id="freeText17528350904070792297" style="display:none">It was such a treat to read “The Red Grouse Tales” by Leslie W.P. Garland. The four short stories within this novel are thoroughly engaging contemporary allegories. I love John Milton’s “Paradise Lost,” thus I was delighted by how deftly Garland interweaves the well-known archangels into these modern-day tales. “The Red Grouse Tales” consists of the most well-done and effective frame narratives I have come across in contemporary pieces of literature. Even more to Garland’s credit, I never considered the frame narrative to be overused across the four stories. The method seemed to be the perfect fit for each story. One of my favorite aspects of this collection of short stories is that the allegories never seemed heavy-handed or forced. I believe that the personalities of each story’s narrators were key to how engaging and relatable the allegories were. I loved the authenticity and likeability of each narrator and the glimpses into their sense of humor and personality quirks as they told their tale. I also appreciated the range of personalities and voices amongst the narrators. Overall, I highly recommend “The Red Grouse Tales” to readers who are interested in contemporary allegories, literature that references religious/religion-related narratives (particularly “Paradise Lost” and other works that involve the archangels), and well-written and effective frame narratives. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17528350904070792297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2103325805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103325805" />
    <a title="Brigitte " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34807917-brigitte"><img alt="Brigitte " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604558413p2/34807917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103325805?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigitte " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigitte " href="/user/show/34807917-brigitte">Brigitte </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34807917-brigitte?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34807917-brigitte?shelf=collection">collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34807917-brigitte?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103325805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9459709173396058642">This is a collection of a good mix of short stories.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>The Crow </i>
</b><br/><br/>The Crow takes place in The Red Grouse Inn where a group of friends meet on Thursdays for a few pints and sharing stories. <br/><br/>This story is told from two different perspectives. Father Patrick and David, one of the regulars.<br/><br/>Reginald Monday aka The Crow is so poor that he is bullied by those more fortunate than him. Father Patrick sees something in him and takes him under his wings. The bullies resent his talents and continue with thei</span>
  <span id="freeText9459709173396058642" style="display:none">This is a collection of a good mix of short stories.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Crow </i>
</b><br /><br />The Crow takes place in The Red Grouse Inn where a group of friends meet on Thursdays for a few pints and sharing stories. <br /><br />This story is told from two different perspectives. Father Patrick and David, one of the regulars.<br /><br />Reginald Monday aka The Crow is so poor that he is bullied by those more fortunate than him. Father Patrick sees something in him and takes him under his wings. The bullies resent his talents and continue with their name calling and humiliation. <br /><br />Then along comes The Crow that befriends Reginald and he starts to change and stands up for himself. He goes on to become successful. As a councillor, he is involved in the building of a dam which means that everything in the village changes. Father Patrick is convinced that he is possessed by the devil and recounts all the negative events. David on the other hand remains objective and realises that parts of the story are distorted. Not everything is as it seems. <br /><br />There are a lot of misunderstandings. The bullies are cruel in their behaviour. Greed rears its ugly head when compensation comes into play. It's a dark story which shows that there is always two sides to a story. <br /><br />The retelling of this short story is very well detailed and intriguing.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The White Hart </i>
</b><br /><br />This short story is told in The Red Grouse Inn, an English Pub, where a group of friends meet regularly for a few pints and a chat. <br /><br />Pete is a bit of a ladies' man who hasn't met the "right one" as yet. He is a Fell Runner, the countryside being like a balm to the his soul. He loves the wild life and the natural environment. His friends like to tease him but it's all in good faith. <br /><br />On this particular Thursday evening, Pete decides to tell a tale about Hartstane Hall, an old estate which has disintegrated over the years. It's about his encounters and one coincidence too many! <br /><br />He starts off with an incident with a white albino deer, white deers are very rare indeed! Then he recounts his first meeting with Raphaella, a young girl in the Harststane Chapel. It's the only part of the estate still standing and Pete goes in to explore. He is impressed with the workmanship but doesn't know much about its history. When Raphaella joins him, he expresses his admiration for the architecture and they go outside where she tells him the history of the estate. <br /><br />She appears to know a lot about what transpired over a century and a half ago in Harstane Hall. The tragedy of Christine, the young girl who inherited the Hall and attracted the wrong attention. It's a sordid story about deceit, greed and murder. He doesn't quite believe what he is hearing. He believes that she has been pulling his legs until he goes for a run in the autumn. Although what he sees then, appears to be totally unrelated, the white deer comes to mind. It's only then that he remembers what Raphaella had asked him. On a closer look his suspicions are confirmed! Coincidence? <br /><br />Do you believe in ghosts? <br /><br />This short story is very well put together. Pete is good natured and gives a vivid account of the events leading up to the end of this story. He has some strange ideas but oddly enough, they are not all that unusual. Everything that he has experienced comes together at the end and it's rather baffling. There is also a morale to this tale. All in all, it's an interesting and intriguing story. I really like the way it ends. Is it another coincidence?<br /><br />If you like ghost stories and looking for something different and easy to read, then this is definitely worth picking up. I quite fancied being in that pub myself that evening as I could actually picture the scene!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Little Dog </i>
</b><br /><br />The Little Dog is one of the stories shared amongst friends over drinks at The Red Grouse pub.<br /><br />This story is narrated by Bill, recalling his days as a forester fifty years ago. <br /><br />Stan has a bad reputation and is not popular with his fellow foresters. He is new to the area and is a bit of an enigma. Bill is paired up with him for a week to clear one of the forests across the lake. He doesn't feel comfortable about the situation, but it's only temporary. <br /><br />On their first journey, they spot a dog, sitting by the road side and he still there on their return journey. There is no sign of his owner and Bill starts to worry when they find him in the same spot for the next few days. Stan's uncaring attitude bothers Bill who starts to ask himself questions about good, bad and evil. He finds himself analysing the subject and ends up going round in circles. What happens on their final journey is a mystery. The nature of the dog is an even bigger mystery. <br /><br />The author paints a good picture of the environment and the occurrences. There are a lot of unanswered questions. Everyone criticises Stan's appearance without really knowing anything about him. What transpires proves that he is an unsavoury character, but there is no closure. It's a philosophical story which leaves it open to interpretation. An interesting read, indeed. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Golden Tup</i>
</b><br /><br />This is another tale recounted by one of the group of friends who regularly meet at The Red Grouse Inn. It's centered around village gossips, hypocrisy and the probability of the presence of an evil being.<br /><br />Verity is a farmer's wife and on this particular occasion she reflects on the sequence of events leading to the demise of a young couple. <br /><br />Constance and Matthew have just moved to this dilapidated farm and they are excited about the renovations. Their dream is to be self sufficient, living off the land. They receive help from the mysterious Gabriel who appears to notice things that they don't. They ignore his advice on a couple of a occasions, but then their good life starts to crumble. In hindsight, they should have listened to him.<br /><br />Verity goes on to relay the fate of another couple who moved to this farm for the same reasons, one hundred and fifty years ago. The similarities in their circumstances are scary! This is further reinforced by the information unearthed by Constance. The root of their troubles appears to be the Golden Tup.<br /><br />This is a rather sad and dark story about what transpired all those years ago and in the present time. It raises a lot of questions about the coincidences and the evil surrounding the these two couples. The narration is vividly described, to the point where I felt uncomfortable and heartbroken about some of the events. An intriguing story which gives food for thoughts. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9459709173396058642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1642708005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1642708005" />
    <a title="Leslie Garland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56010014-leslie-garland"><img alt="Leslie Garland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465419387p2/56010014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1642708005?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie Garland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie Garland" href="/user/show/56010014-leslie-garland">Leslie Garland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642708005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3070694202177155321">I honestly can't remember when I first came up with idea of a group of friends telling each other tales in a pub, but it was that idea which gave rise to The Red Grouse Tales - The Red Grouse being the name of the pub - and as for the tales; these I wanted to be slightly fantastic whilst at the same time being vaguely plausible, modern day fairy stories if you like. This concept is not new, what I hope is new is that of a more modern take on old ideas, mixed in with a bit of thought provocation </span>
  <span id="freeText3070694202177155321" style="display:none">I honestly can't remember when I first came up with idea of a group of friends telling each other tales in a pub, but it was that idea which gave rise to The Red Grouse Tales - The Red Grouse being the name of the pub - and as for the tales; these I wanted to be slightly fantastic whilst at the same time being vaguely plausible, modern day fairy stories if you like. This concept is not new, what I hope is new is that of a more modern take on old ideas, mixed in with a bit of thought provocation resulting in, I trust, a good read. <br />The four stories in this first collection are deliberately different, I hope sit well together and are:- The Little Dog, The Crow, The Golden Tup and The White Hart. Each tale is available individually and I suggest you take a look at my reviews of each (on this site) if you want to know more about them and hence about this collection, and / or have a look at my website <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lesliegarland.com">http://www.lesliegarland.com</a><br />I hope you have as much fun reading them as I had writing them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3070694202177155321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2122607092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122607092" />
    <a title="Michelle Ryles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20375087-michelle-ryles"><img alt="Michelle Ryles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570188936p2/20375087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2122607092?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Ryles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Ryles" href="/user/show/20375087-michelle-ryles">Michelle Ryles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20375087-michelle-ryles?shelf=galleys-read">galleys-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2122607092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16521848192669925581">I've deliberated for quite a while over how to both rate and review The Red Grouse Tales. As it is an anthology of four of Leslie W.P. Garland's short stories, I will review the book as a whole and as separate stories but as with all short stories, do bear in mind that I may have liked a story that may not appeal to others and vice versa. Such is life and it would be boring if we all liked the same things! <br/><br/>I loved the idea of The Red Grouse Tales: stories that friends told each other over a pint</span>
  <span id="freeText16521848192669925581" style="display:none">I've deliberated for quite a while over how to both rate and review The Red Grouse Tales. As it is an anthology of four of Leslie W.P. Garland's short stories, I will review the book as a whole and as separate stories but as with all short stories, do bear in mind that I may have liked a story that may not appeal to others and vice versa. Such is life and it would be boring if we all liked the same things! <br /><br />I loved the idea of The Red Grouse Tales: stories that friends told each other over a pint in their local pub. The four stories are: The Little Dog, The Crow, The Golden Tup and The White Hart. Each story is different and surprisingly thought provoking with hints of theology, philosophy and fantasy interwoven into them.<br /><br />The Little Dog kicks off the anthology with a dark supernatural mystery. I felt chilled by the character of Stan and feared for Bill's safety when he was partnered with him at work. As the end of their shift together drew near, I felt relieved for Bill at the thought of him parting ways with Stan and his black heart. I found the story quite slow to start but I loved the character of the little dog sitting on the roadside and Bill's pleasure at seeing him in the same spot every day. The Little Dog gets a 3 star rating from me.<br /><br />Now on to the elephant in the room, or The Crow. Oh dear, I really didn't get on with this story at all. The main problem for me was Father Patrick's broad Irish words being written phonetically and it hurt my eyes and my brain to read it. I found it so hard going that I couldn't really take in the story as I was too busy trying to decipher what this Irish, or he could even have been Jamaican, priest was saying. I just have to give two little examples:<br /><br /><i>Dese men t'inks dat dey know what's best for udder men... </i><br /><br /><i>T' be sure, dere are dem dat want t' change d' world, change d' world t' a bedder place, and t' be sure maybe dey starts out wid dat intention...</i><br /><br />I felt that the way the speech was written and the constant repetition of 't' be sure' to be a bit condescending. I would have felt the same had an attempt been made to write Scottish or even Geordie accents into the written word. I just wanted Dave to put a pillow over Father Patrick's face to put me out of my misery. Sadly, The Crow only gets 1 star from me.<br /><br />Thankfully, I never give up on a book so I laboured on and I was delighted to find that the next story, The Golden Tup, really appealed to me. It's mysterious, intriguing and very dark; there's definitely evil lurking in Burnhope farm and I loved the way that Verity told the tale - I could imagine her recounting the story with a torch held up to her face to add to the creepiness. The Golden Tup gets a solid 4 star rating.<br /><br />For me, Leslie W.P. Garland definitely saved the best to last; The White Hart left me with goosebumps and I thought the writing was excellent. It was slightly spooky, philosophical and humorous, with Pete Montague appearing as a modern day Romeo. I loved how the three threads of the story were plaited together with not a hair out of place and I would easily give this story a 5 star rating.<br /><br />Variety is the spice of life and from the various ratings I have given each story, you can see that there are quite a variety of stories in The Red Grouse Tales. There really is something for everyone and although I clearly enjoyed some stories more than others, I think that's normal in a collection of vastly different tales. I would definitely recommend you pick up The Golden Tup and The White Hart, if you're a fan of novellas.<br /><br />I chose to read an ARC and this is my honest and unbiased opinion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16521848192669925581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209952508" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24866033-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578432846p2/24866033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209952508?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/24866033-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28571709-the-little-dog-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209952508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15101604618656348307">I’ll be honest, this is a difficult one for me to review. On one hand, the novellas within The Red Grouse Tales were so well written. They were rich in detail and characterisation; for example, the dialogue in The Crow was written phonetically whenever the Irish Father Patrick spoke which added another element to the reading experience and must have taken dedication and time to write. But on the other hand, I struggled to get into them. Despite all the positives, some of which I have already men</span>
  <span id="freeText15101604618656348307" style="display:none">I’ll be honest, this is a difficult one for me to review. On one hand, the novellas within The Red Grouse Tales were so well written. They were rich in detail and characterisation; for example, the dialogue in The Crow was written phonetically whenever the Irish Father Patrick spoke which added another element to the reading experience and must have taken dedication and time to write. But on the other hand, I struggled to get into them. Despite all the positives, some of which I have already mentioned, I didn’t get a feel for the characters and felt as if I had to read between the lines a lot. There isn’t anything wrong with this, there is nothing wrong with authors wanting their readers to really think about what they are reading, but personally, I felt there was a little too much thinking and not enough reading for me.<br /><br />The stories were so rich in detail and well written, I think these 4 novellas where the perfect length to really compliment Leslie Garland’s writing. They were so immersive and detailed that I think being any longer would have been a detriment to the author’s writing style. I also enjoyed the slightly old fashioned tone that these stories had.<br /><br />I don’t think anyone can deny that Leslie Garland is a very talented writer, but these stories just weren’t for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15101604618656348307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13525776860831119454" style="display:none">4 intriguing with a touch of supernatural having religious and moral undertones are told when some friends meet at a pub and each one tells a tale every time they meet.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742005518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5029532580989175526"><br/>“Are we all born innocent, or are people born that way? Born evil?” A quote from the first story, but seems to carry though the rest<br/><br/>The stories are well thought out. Three of the stories are well written. I did have some trouble with The Crow. It had a lot to do with the dialect. Although endearing at first, it became hard to follow with it being written out how the accent would sound.  Sometimes it’s easier to explain how the person speaks vs writing words out like that. Show vs tell comes to m</span>
  <span id="freeText5029532580989175526" style="display:none"><br />“Are we all born innocent, or are people born that way? Born evil?” A quote from the first story, but seems to carry though the rest<br /><br />The stories are well thought out. Three of the stories are well written. I did have some trouble with The Crow. It had a lot to do with the dialect. Although endearing at first, it became hard to follow with it being written out how the accent would sound.  Sometimes it’s easier to explain how the person speaks vs writing words out like that. Show vs tell comes to mind.<br /><br />The stories definitely had biblical undertones with a lot based on good vs evil. If you’re not one who enjoys religious themed stories, these might not be the stories for you. It reminds me of a set of short stories my mother used to read to me. They all focused on choices and impacts in life. Much like these stories.<br /><br />I will say the stories are a bit slow. It takes quite a while to get to the punch and to see where the stories are going. But nonetheless, was an enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5029532580989175526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

What I liked most about this book, were the tangents the writer goes on in nearly every story. Only one of the stories did not speak to me, other than that I felt that each one had its purpose and place in the book. </span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_18334354'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18334354-quantum-roots"><img alt="Quantum Roots (Quantum Roots, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1376602412l/18334354._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3XuVILCuHHUtktri5dQhkcFceE3D4MOU6VdySMFoR3R+G+Wfj67qYtJlh6J1kWoPKlWIVKUvPcEZPI4Hz0SY3w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kx/DmgK7gGFoZJcvJgjka6vU9yq0t9cn1jLh3Ad64I4wf7MlPbt2dpeTym+2Ta/1QN0HM9J4KXImWR2TCVY/JQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Snyder did when he joined it;• German atrocities toward captured crew and civilians;• behind-the-scenes stories of the Belgium civilians who risked all to save American flyers who were in the air one moment, spiraling down in flames the next;• creation and dedication of the monument to the Susan Ruth and its crew located in Macquenoise, Belgium in 1989.Shot Down was created from the vast number of letters and journals of Howard Snyder; diaries of men and women on the ground who rescued, sheltered and hid the crew; and interviews conducted by historians. Centered around the 306th Bomb Group in Thurleigh, England, it is informative, insightful and captivating.For most, 70 years is a long time ago. World War II fades in importance as each year goes by. Shot Down moves history out of the footnotes into reality, keeping the stories of real people alive as they experience being shot down. You are there, almost holding your breath as Lt. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16923719377603192084">I didn't start out in a career in writing; I qualified as a Chartered Civil Engineer. As an engineer I worked for several years on projects in the UK, the Far East and Africa. During this period I won the Institution of Civil Engineers “Miller Prize” for a paper on tunnelling. Perhaps my first foray in to writing? It was a pretty dry technical piece. However my experience in tunnelling has given m</span>
  <span id="freeText16923719377603192084" style="display:none">I didn't start out in a career in writing; I qualified as a Chartered Civil Engineer. As an engineer I worked for several years on projects in the UK, the Far East and Africa. During this period I won the Institution of Civil Engineers “Miller Prize” for a paper on tunnelling. Perhaps my first foray in to writing? It was a pretty dry technical piece. However my experience in tunnelling has given me an exciting idea for a story which I hope will be a lot more fun than my engineering paper. Changing times resulted in a change in direction and after qualifying as an Associate Member of both the British Institute of Professional Photography and the Royal Photographic Society, started my own stock photograph library (the first in N.E.England) and wrote for the trade press. The Internet was new in those days and not very reliable. So an unexpected break in my Internet connection fortuitously presented the time to make a start on a long cherished project of a series of novella length stories, and the first story of 'The Red Grouse Tales', was drafted. Three more 'tales' have followed. Since then I have completed a further three 'tales' and a novel. Right now I am trying to complete a second batch of 'tales' and planning my next novel. I live with my wife in Northumberland, England. More information on my website<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lesliegarland.com">http://www.lesliegarland.com</a> <br />Follow me on Twitter <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/LeslieWPGarland">https://twitter.com/LeslieWPGarland</a> <br />FaceBook; you'll find me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16923719377603192084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
